	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Netherlands national football team</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the men's team. For the women's team, see <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Netherlands women&#39;s national football team">Netherlands women's national football team</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Holland football team" redirects here. For the football club in Essex, see <a href="/wiki/Holland_F.C." title="Holland F.C.">Holland F.C.</a></div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Men's national association football team representing the Netherlands</div>

<p>The <b>Netherlands national football team</b><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;B&#93;</a></sup> has represented the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> in international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> matches since 1905. The national team is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Football_Association" title="Royal Dutch Football Association">Royal Dutch Football Association</a> (KNVB), which is a part of <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>, and under the jurisdiction of <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> the governing body for <a href="/wiki/Football_in_the_Netherlands" title="Football in the Netherlands">football in the Netherlands</a>. Most of the Netherlands' home matches are played at the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Arena" title="Johan Cruyff Arena">Johan Cruyff Arena</a> and the <a href="/wiki/De_Kuip" title="De Kuip">Stadion Feijenoord</a>. The team is colloquially referred to as <i>Het Nederlands Elftal</i> (The Dutch Eleven) or <i>Oranje</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Orange-Nassau" title="House of Orange-Nassau">House of Orange-Nassau</a>. Like the country itself, the team is sometimes (also colloquially) referred to as <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_(toponymy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Netherlands (toponymy)"><b>Holland</b></a>. The fan club is known as "Het Oranje Legioen".<sup id="cite_ref-HetLegioen_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HetLegioen-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Netherlands has competed in ten <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a>, appearing in the finals three times (in <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974</a>, <a href="/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1978 FIFA World Cup">1978</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010</a>). They have also appeared in nine <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA European Championships">UEFA European Championships</a>, winning the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">1988</a> tournament in West Germany. Additionally, the team won a bronze medal at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the Summer Olympics">Olympic tournament</a> in <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1908_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1908 Summer Olympics">1908</a>, <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1912_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1912 Summer Olympics">1912</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1920_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1920 Summer Olympics">1920</a>. The Netherlands has long-standing football rivalries with neighbors Belgium and Germany.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands_national_football_team" title="History of the Netherlands national football team">History of the Netherlands national football team</a></div>
<h3><span id="Beginnings:_1905.E2.80.931969"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings:_1905–1969">Beginnings: 1905–1969</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beginnings: 1905–1969">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg/250px-Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg/375px-Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg/500px-Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3590" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nederlands_elftal_1905_colorized.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1905 Netherlands team</div></div></div>
<p>The Netherlands played their first international match in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> against <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> on 30 April 1905. The players were selected by a five-member commission from the Dutch football association. After 90 minutes, the score was 1–1. Because the match was for the Coupe van den Abeele it went into overtime, during which <a href="/wiki/Eddy_de_Neve" title="Eddy de Neve">Eddy de Neve</a> scored three times, making the score 4–1 for the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Some historians attribute one of the goals scored to <a href="/wiki/Willem_Hesselink" title="Willem Hesselink">Willem Hesselink</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1908, the Netherlands competed in their first official tournament appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1908_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1908 Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. They received a bronze medal after losing to <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Olympic_football_team" title="Great Britain Olympic football team">Great Britain</a> in the semifinals, before defeating <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> in the bronze medal match 2–0.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> At the Olympic Games in 1912 and 1920, the Dutch finished with the bronze medal as they lost to Denmark and Belgium in the respective tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Dutch reached the semi-finals at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1924_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1924 Summer Olympics">1924 Summer Olympics</a> in Paris after winning against <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_football_team" title="Romania national football team">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Free State national football team">Ireland</a>. In the semi-final, they gave up a one-goal lead, scored by <a href="/wiki/Kees_Pijl" title="Kees Pijl">Kees Pijl</a>, to lose 2–1 and were relegated to the third-place playoff for the fourth time,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> losing to Sweden in a replay.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Holland_-_Switzerland_-_Football_World_Cup_1934.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Holland_-_Switzerland_-_Football_World_Cup_1934.jpg/220px-Holland_-_Switzerland_-_Football_World_Cup_1934.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Holland_-_Switzerland_-_Football_World_Cup_1934.jpg/330px-Holland_-_Switzerland_-_Football_World_Cup_1934.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Holland_-_Switzerland_-_Football_World_Cup_1934.jpg/440px-Holland_-_Switzerland_-_Football_World_Cup_1934.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="898" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Holland_-_Switzerland_-_Football_World_Cup_1934.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netherlands make their way out to face Switzerland at the <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1934 FIFA World Cup">1934 FIFA World Cup</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>After being eliminated in the first round at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1928_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1928 Summer Olympics">1928 Summer Olympics</a> on home turf,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> they skipped the first World Cup in 1930 due to the cost of travel from Europe to South America.<sup id="cite_ref-FIFA1930_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA1930-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The team made their first appearance at a <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1934 FIFA World Cup">1934</a> where they took on Switzerland. <a href="/wiki/Kick_Smit" title="Kick Smit">Kick Smit</a> was the first goalscorer for the Netherlands in a World Cup. The team was eliminated in the opening round by Switzerland 3–2.<sup id="cite_ref-fiedler_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fiedler-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> A second appearance at the <a href="/wiki/1938_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1938 FIFA World Cup">1938 World Cup</a> resulted in a first-round elimination against <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team" title="Czechoslovakia national football team">Czechoslovakia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the Second World War, the Dutch qualified for only two international tournaments before the 1970s. The <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1948_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1948 Summer Olympics">1948 Summer Olympics</a> in Great Britain and the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1952_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1952 Summer Olympics">1952 Summer Olympics</a> in Finland. They faced early elimination losing to the hosts in 1948<sup id="cite_ref-1948OLY_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1948OLY-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-1952OLY_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1952OLY-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Total_Football_in_the_1970s">Total Football in the 1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Total Football in the 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 1970s, <a href="/wiki/Total_Football" title="Total Football">Total Football</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Totaalvoetbal</i>) was invented, pioneered by <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> and led by playmaker <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a> and national team head coach <a href="/wiki/Rinus_Michels" title="Rinus Michels">Rinus Michels</a>. The Dutch made significant strides, qualifying for two World Cup finals in the decade. <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Alberto_Torres" title="Carlos Alberto Torres">Carlos Alberto</a>, captain of the Brazilian team that won the <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">1970 FIFA World Cup</a> said, "The only team I've seen that did things differently was Holland at <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">the 1974 World Cup in Germany</a>. Since then everything looks more or less the same to me&#160;... Their 'carousel' style of play was amazing to watch and marvelous for the game."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1974, the Netherlands beat both Brazil and <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> in the second group stage, reaching the final for the first time in their history. However, they lost to <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> in <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1974 FIFA World Cup Final">the final</a> in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, despite having gone up 1–0 through <a href="/wiki/Johan_Neeskens" title="Johan Neeskens">Johan Neeskens</a>' early <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kick</a> before a German had even touched the ball. However, a converted penalty by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Breitner" title="Paul Breitner">Paul Breitner</a> and the winner from <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Gerd Müller</a>, led to a victory for the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-74WC_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74WC-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311,_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM,_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM%2C_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="793" data-file-height="451" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N0716-0311,_Fu%C3%9Fball-WM,_BRD_-_Niederlande_2-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Dutch team before their 1–2 loss against <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> in the final of the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1976" title="UEFA Euro 1976">1976 European Championship</a> the Netherlands qualified for their first <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">European Championship</a> after beating Belgium in the quarterfinals. They were matched in the semifinals by Czechoslovakia who kept Cruyff and Van Hanegem within arms-length of another player as they defeated the Dutch in overtime.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The Dutch finished in third place after defeating the hosts (Yugoslavia) in overtime.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1978, the Netherlands qualified for the World Cup in Argentina. The team was missing Johan Cruyff due to a kidnapping attempt,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Wim_van_Hanegem" class="mw-redirect" title="Wim van Hanegem">Wim van Hanegem</a>. But the squad still had players like <a href="/wiki/Jan_Jongbloed" title="Jan Jongbloed">Jan Jongbloed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wim_Suurbier" title="Wim Suurbier">Wim Suurbier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Krol" title="Ruud Krol">Ruud Krol</a> from the previous World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> After finishing runner-up in Group 4 behind <a href="/wiki/Peru_national_football_team" title="Peru national football team">Peru</a>, they recorded wins against Austria and <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> to set up <a href="/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1978 FIFA World Cup Final">a final with Argentina</a>. After a controversial start, with Argentina questioning the plaster cast on <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_van_de_Kerkhof" title="René van de Kerkhof">René van de Kerkhof</a>'s wrist, the match headed to extra time where the Dutch lost 3–1 after two <a href="/wiki/Extra_time" class="mw-redirect" title="Extra time">extra time</a> goals from <a href="/wiki/Mario_Kempes" title="Mario Kempes">Mario Kempes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bertoni" title="Daniel Bertoni">Daniel Bertoni</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78WC_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78WC-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Failure_before_European_champions">Failure before European champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Failure before European champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1980" title="UEFA Euro 1980">Euro '80</a> was the last tournament for which the Total Football team qualified. Despite the tournament format being expanded that year they did not advance past the group stage as they finished behind Czechoslovakia by goal difference.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Veterans such as Krol and Rensenbrink retired soon afterwards and the Dutch team hit a low point in their history: they missed the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 World Cup</a> in Spain, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1984" title="UEFA Euro 1984">Euro 1984</a> in France, and the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 World Cup</a> in Mexico. They failed qualifying for Euro 1984 by virtue of goals scored when <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> scored twelve in the final game against <a href="/wiki/Malta_national_football_team" title="Malta national football team">Malta</a>. Because both teams had the same goal difference (+16), Spain qualified having scored two more goals than the Dutch.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> During the qualification stage for the 1986 World Cup the Dutch finished in second place and advanced to the playoffs against neighbors Belgium. After losing the first leg 1–0 in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, they held a 2–0 lead at <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> with a few minutes remaining. But <a href="/wiki/Georges_Grun" class="mw-redirect" title="Georges Grun">Georges Grun</a>'s header in the 84th minute resulted in the Netherlands elimination as Belgium advanced to the World Cup on <a href="/wiki/Away_goals_rule" title="Away goals rule">away goals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1986WCQ_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1986WCQ-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Beker.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/De_Beker.jpg/170px-De_Beker.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/De_Beker.jpg/255px-De_Beker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/De_Beker.jpg/340px-De_Beker.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Beker.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1988 trophy on display in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Persconferentie_ivm_vertrek_van_bondscoach_Kees_Rijvers_en_de_opvolging_van_hem_,_Bestanddeelnr_933-1361.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Persconferentie_ivm_vertrek_van_bondscoach_Kees_Rijvers_en_de_opvolging_van_hem_%2C_Bestanddeelnr_933-1361.jpg/160px-Persconferentie_ivm_vertrek_van_bondscoach_Kees_Rijvers_en_de_opvolging_van_hem_%2C_Bestanddeelnr_933-1361.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Persconferentie_ivm_vertrek_van_bondscoach_Kees_Rijvers_en_de_opvolging_van_hem_%2C_Bestanddeelnr_933-1361.jpg/240px-Persconferentie_ivm_vertrek_van_bondscoach_Kees_Rijvers_en_de_opvolging_van_hem_%2C_Bestanddeelnr_933-1361.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Persconferentie_ivm_vertrek_van_bondscoach_Kees_Rijvers_en_de_opvolging_van_hem_%2C_Bestanddeelnr_933-1361.jpg/320px-Persconferentie_ivm_vertrek_van_bondscoach_Kees_Rijvers_en_de_opvolging_van_hem_%2C_Bestanddeelnr_933-1361.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2445" data-file-height="3682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Persconferentie_ivm_vertrek_van_bondscoach_Kees_Rijvers_en_de_opvolging_van_hem_,_Bestanddeelnr_933-1361.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rinus_Michels" title="Rinus Michels">Rinus Michels</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rinus Michels returned, with his technical assistant Joris van Beek, to coach the team for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">Euro 1988</a> in West Germany. After losing the first group match against the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_national_football_team" title="Soviet Union national football team">Soviet Union</a> (1–0), the Netherlands qualified for the semi-final by defeating <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> 3–1 (with a hat-trick by the tournament's top scorer <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Marco van Basten</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> (1–0). For many Dutch football supporters, the most important match in the tournament was the semi-final against West Germany, the host country, considered as revenge for the 1974 World Cup final (also in West Germany). Van Basten scored in the 89th minute to sink the German side.<sup id="cite_ref-Riv_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Riv-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The Netherlands won the final with a victory over the USSR with a header by <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a> and a volley by Van Basten. This was the national team's first major tournament win.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Netherlands was one of the favourites for the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 World Cup</a> tournament in Italy until <a href="/wiki/Thijs_Libregts" title="Thijs Libregts">Thijs Libregts</a> was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Leo_Beenhakker" title="Leo Beenhakker">Leo Beenhakker</a> in a late management switch.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> After this, the Dutch scored only two goals in the group stage which featured England, <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a> and the Republic of Ireland. After finishing the group stage with identical records, the Netherlands and the Republic of Ireland drew lots to determine which team would finish second. The Netherlands had the tougher draw against West Germany, while the Republic of Ireland took Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-OddTieBreakers_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OddTieBreakers-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The match against West Germany is mostly remembered for the spitting-incident involving <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rudi_V%C3%B6ller" title="Rudi Völler">Rudi Völler</a> as the Netherlands were defeated 2–1.<sup id="cite_ref-Riv_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Riv-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The team reached the semifinals in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1992" title="UEFA Euro 1992">Euro 1992</a> in Sweden, which was noted for the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Bergkamp" title="Dennis Bergkamp">Dennis Bergkamp</a>. They were eliminated by eventual champions <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>, however, when <a href="/wiki/Peter_Schmeichel" title="Peter Schmeichel">Peter Schmeichel</a> saved Van Basten's kick in the penalty shootout.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> This was Van Basten's last major tournament. He suffered a serious ankle injury shortly after, and eventually retired at age 30 in 1995. It was also the last hurrah for Rinus Michels, who returned for one final spell in charge of the team before retiring for good after the tournament ended.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dick_Advocaat" title="Dick Advocaat">Dick Advocaat</a> took over from Michels on the understanding that he would be replaced by Johan Cruyff the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-Independent_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> But after talks between Cruyff and the KNVB broke down, Advocaat remained in charge of the national team for the World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 World Cup</a> in the United States, in the absence of the injured Van Basten and the <a href="/wiki/Striker_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Striker (association football)">striker</a> Ruud Gullit,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Dennis Bergkamp led the team with three goals and the Netherlands advanced to the quarter-finals, where they lost 3–2 to eventual champions Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-1994WC_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1994WC-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Golden_Teams:_1996.E2.80.932014"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Golden_Teams:_1996–2014">Golden Teams: 1996–2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Golden Teams: 1996–2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg/220px-Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg/330px-Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg/440px-Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="552" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotland-holland_euro_96.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netherlands at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">Euro 96</a> match against Scotland at the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Park" title="Villa Park">Villa Park</a> stadium in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, England</div></div></div>
<p>After finishing second in their <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">Euro 1996</a> group, they played <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> in the quarter-finals. With the score nil all, the match went to penalties. <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Seedorf" title="Clarence Seedorf">Clarence Seedorf</a>'s shot in the fourth round was stopped by French goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Lama" title="Bernard Lama">Bernard Lama</a>, but the goal by Laurent Blanc eliminated the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> After they finished top of the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_7" title="1998 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group 7">qualifying group</a>, they were drawn in Group E of the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 World Cup</a>. With the Dutch team featuring Dennis Bergkamp, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Overmars" title="Marc Overmars">Marc Overmars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Cocu" title="Phillip Cocu">Phillip Cocu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Davids" title="Edgar Davids">Edgar Davids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_de_Boer" title="Frank de Boer">Frank de Boer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_de_Boer" title="Ronald de Boer">Ronald de Boer</a> and Kluivert, they reached the semifinals where they again lost on penalties, this time to Brazil.  Falling behind early in the second half before an 87th-minute goal from <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a> gave the Dutch fans hope,  they lost 4–2 on penalties, and then lost the third-place playoff to <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Soon afterwards, manager <a href="/wiki/Guus_Hiddink" title="Guus Hiddink">Guus Hiddink</a> resigned to be replaced by Frank Rijkaard. The Netherlands co-hosted <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a> with Belgium and won all three games in the group stage and then defeated <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro_national_football_team" title="Serbia and Montenegro national football team">FR Yugoslavia</a> 6–1 in the quarter-finals. In the semifinals, Italian goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Toldo" title="Francesco Toldo">Francesco Toldo</a> made two penalty shootout saves to eliminate the Netherlands. The team failed to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 World Cup</a> after crucial losses to <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> and the Republic of Ireland, prompting manager <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG/325px-Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG" decoding="async" width="325" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG/488px-Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG/650px-Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1143" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Training_Netherlands_in_Freiburg.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netherlands at the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>Dick Advocaat became the national coach for the Netherlands for the second time in January 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Dual_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dual-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> His first match was a 1–1 draw against England in Rotterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-ned_2002_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ned_2002-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The national team finished second place in their <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004_qualifying_Group_3" title="UEFA Euro 2004 qualifying Group 3">qualifying group</a> for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">2004 Euros</a>. Having to play in the playoffs after losing to the Czech Republic,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> they knocked off <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> with a 6–0 win in the second leg to qualify for the 2004 tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The tournament saw the Dutch make it to the semifinals where they lost to the hosts in Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Heavy criticism of his handling of the national team lead Advocaat to quit.<sup id="cite_ref-Quits_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quits-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Netherlands qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> under new manager Marco van Basten. They were eliminated in the second round after losing 1–0 to Portugal. The match produced 16 <a href="/wiki/Fouls_and_misconduct_(association_football)" title="Fouls and misconduct (association football)">yellow cards</a>, matching the World Cup record for most cautions in one game set in 2002, and set a new World Cup record of <a href="/wiki/Fouls_and_misconduct_(association_football)" title="Fouls and misconduct (association football)">four red cards</a>, two per side;<sup id="cite_ref-abc_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> it was nicknamed "the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nuremberg_(2006_FIFA_World_Cup)" title="Battle of Nuremberg (2006 FIFA World Cup)">Battle of Nuremberg</a>" by the press.<sup id="cite_ref-Nuremberg_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nuremberg-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Despite criticism surrounding his selection policy and the lack of attacking football from his team, Van Basten was offered a two-year extension to his contract by the KNVB. This allowed him to serve as national coach during <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">Euro 2008</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The Netherlands qualified for Euro 2008, where they were drawn in the "<a href="/wiki/Group_of_Death" class="mw-redirect" title="Group of Death">Group of Death</a>", together with France, Italy and Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> They began with a 3–0 win over world champions Italy in <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">Bern</a>, their first victory over the Italians since 1978. They then beat France by 4-1 to qualify for the second round, and went on winning the group on nine points after beating Romania 2-0 with (mainly) their reserve players. However, they then lost in the quarter-finals to Guus Hiddink's <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a> 3–1, with <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a> scoring an 86th-minute equaliser to force extra time, where the Russians scored twice. Following the tournament, Van Basten resigned having accepted the role at Ajax.<sup id="cite_ref-Van_Basten_takes_Ajax_role_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Basten_takes_Ajax_role-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG/220px-Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG/330px-Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG/440px-Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2523" data-file-height="1523" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Holland_-_France_Euro_2008_entrance_into_stadium.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netherlands&#160;– France at Euro 2008</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg/220px-Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg/330px-Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg/440px-Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1532" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_-_Denmark_WC2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netherlands&#160;– Denmark at the 2010 World Cup</div></div></div>
<p>Under new coach <a href="/wiki/Bert_van_Marwijk" title="Bert van Marwijk">Bert van Marwijk</a>, the Dutch went on to secure a 100% record in <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_9" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group 9">their World Cup 2010 qualification campaign</a> to qualify for the World Cup. After they had comfortably qualified with maximum points in Group E<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia_national_football_team" title="Slovakia national football team">Slovakia</a><sup id="cite_ref-NEDVSSVK_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDVSSVK-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> in the round of 16, they took on Brazil in the quarter-finals. After trailing 1–0 at half-time, <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Sneijder" title="Wesley Sneijder">Wesley Sneijder</a> scored two goals in the second half to advance the team to the semis where they defeated <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a> 3–2.<sup id="cite_ref-NEDVSBRA_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDVSBRA-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> They advanced to their first World Cup final since 1978 but <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2010 FIFA World Cup Final">fell to Spain 1–0</a> after midfielder <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Iniesta" title="Andrés Iniesta">Andrés Iniesta</a> scored in extra time.<sup id="cite_ref-2010WCF_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010WCF-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> From August to September 2011, the team was ranked number one in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> becoming the second national football team, after Spain, to top the rankings without previously winning a World Cup.
</p><p>For <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a>, the Netherlands were placed in Group B with Germany, Portugal and Denmark, dubbed the tournament's "Group of Death".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The Netherlands lost all three of its matches. Dutch football legend Johan Cruyff criticised the team's star players for poor build up play and sloppy execution of the easy passes.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Manager Bert van Marwijk resigned after the disappointment.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Louis van Gaal became the manager for the second time. In the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2014 World Cup UEFA qualifying round</a>, the Netherlands won nine games and drew one, topping the group and earning automatic qualification. They were drawn into <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_B" title="2014 FIFA World Cup Group B">Group B</a>, alongside Spain, <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_football_team" title="Chile national football team">Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a>. The team avenged their 2010 defeat by defeating title holders Spain 5–1 in their opening match, with <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a> scoring two goals each and <a href="/wiki/Stefan_de_Vrij" title="Stefan de Vrij">Stefan de Vrij</a> the other.<sup id="cite_ref-NEDESP2014_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDESP2014-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_FIFIA_World_Cup,_Semi_final,_NED-ARG(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg/220px-2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg/330px-2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg/440px-2014_FIFIA_World_Cup%2C_Semi_final%2C_NED-ARG%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_FIFIA_World_Cup,_Semi_final,_NED-ARG(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Dutch team leaves the field after losing to Argentina at the 2014 World Cup.</div></div></div>
<p>After finishing top of Group B, the Dutch defeated <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> 2–1 in the round of 16, with Wesley Sneijder equalising late in the match and <a href="/wiki/Klaas-Jan_Huntelaar" title="Klaas-Jan Huntelaar">Klaas-Jan Huntelaar</a> scoring a controversial penalty after a foul on Arjen Robben in stoppage time.<sup id="cite_ref-NEDvMEX_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDvMEX-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In the quarter-finals, where they faced <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">Costa Rica</a>, the Dutch had many shots on goal but could not score; the match finished in a 0–0 draw after extra time. The Netherlands won the ensuing penalty shootout 4–3. This was due in large part to backup goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Tim_Krul" title="Tim Krul">Tim Krul</a> who was brought on just before the end of extra time and made two saves. This marked the first time in World Cup history a goalkeeper was brought onto the field solely to participate in a shootout.<sup id="cite_ref-CRCvNED_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRCvNED-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The semi-final against Argentina saw the Netherlands having a good chance to score from Arjen Robben while containing <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a> as it remained scoreless after extra time. However, in penalty kicks, the Dutch were eliminated 4–2, with <a href="/wiki/Ron_Vlaar" title="Ron Vlaar">Ron Vlaar</a> and Wesley Sneijder having their spot kicks saved by <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Romero" title="Sergio Romero">Sergio Romero</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The Netherlands won the third-place match against hosts Brazil. Van Gaal, who successfully motivated the team after their semi-final elimination,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> received praise for getting more out of the young and inexperienced Netherlands squad than many expected.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Decline_and_recovery:_2014.E2.80.93"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_and_recovery:_2014–">Decline and recovery: 2014–</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Decline and recovery: 2014–">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guus Hiddink followed Van Gaal as manager for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">Euro 2016 qualifying</a> campaign. On 29 June 2015, Hiddink resigned and was succeeded by assistant <a href="/wiki/Danny_Blind" title="Danny Blind">Danny Blind</a>. The Netherlands finished fourth in their group failing to qualify for the European Championship for the first time since 1984, and missing a major tournament for the first time since the 2002 World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The team's poor form continued into the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2018 World Cup qualifiers</a>, eventually resulting in Blind being dismissed after a 2–0 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a> in March 2017. After the return of Dick Advocaat as coach, the Netherlands failed to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, finishing third in <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_A" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group A">Group A</a> behind France and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2018, Advocaat was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Koeman" title="Ronald Koeman">Ronald Koeman</a>, on a contract until the summer of 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The Netherlands qualified for League A in the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Nations_League" title="2018–19 UEFA Nations League">UEFA Nations League</a> where they would qualify to the final four after drawing with Germany on the final match day, beating France by head-to-head records.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_image">Team image</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Team image">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kits_and_crest">Kits and crest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Kits and crest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/30px-Commons-logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="30" height="40" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/45px-Commons-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/59px-Commons-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1376" /></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikimedia Commons has media related to <i><b><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team_kits" class="extiw" title="commons:Netherlands national football team kits">Netherlands national football team kits</a></b></i>.</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/220px-Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/330px-Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/440px-Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3012" data-file-height="1668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_fans_-_2006_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch fans wearing the <a href="/wiki/Oranjegekte" title="Oranjegekte">traditional orange</a> colours at a <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> match in <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Netherlands national football team famously plays in bright orange shirts. Orange is the historic <a href="/wiki/National_colours" title="National colours">national colour</a> of the Netherlands, originating from one of the many titles of the ruling head of state, <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Orange" title="Prince of Orange">Prince of Orange</a>. The current Dutch away shirt is blue. The lion on the crest is the Netherlands' national and royal animal and has been on the crest since 1907 when they won 3–1 over Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> is the national team's <a href="/wiki/Kit_(association_football)" title="Kit (association football)">kit</a> provider, a sponsorship that began in 1996 and is contracted to continue until at least 2026.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Before that the team was supplied by <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lotto_Sport_Italia" title="Lotto Sport Italia">Lotto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Germany%E2%80%93Netherlands_football_rivalry" title="Germany–Netherlands football rivalry">Germany–Netherlands football rivalry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries_derby" title="Low Countries derby">Low Countries derby</a></div>
<p>Deeply rooted in Dutch <a href="/wiki/Anti-German_sentiment" title="Anti-German sentiment">anti-German sentiment</a> due to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands_(1939%E2%80%931945)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Netherlands (1939–1945)">occupation of the Netherlands by Germany</a> during World War II, the Netherlands' long-time football rival is Germany. Beginning in 1974, when the Dutch lost the 1974 World Cup to West Germany in the final, the rivalry between the two nations has become one of the best-known <a href="/wiki/List_of_association_football_club_rivalries_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="List of association football club rivalries by country">in international football</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To a lesser extent, the Netherlands maintains a rivalry with their other neighbour, Belgium; a Belgium–Netherlands fixture is referred to as a <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries_derby" title="Low Countries derby">Low Countries derby</a>. They have played in 126 matches as of May&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> with the two competing against each other regularly between 1905 and 1964. This has diminished due to the rise of semi-professional football.<sup id="cite_ref-DerbyBelNed_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DerbyBelNed-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> More recently, the Netherlands have also developed a rivalry with Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-espnfc_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnfc-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> This recent rivalry began in 2010, when Spain defeated the Netherlands 1–0 after extra time in the final match of the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>. Four years later, the Netherlands routed Spain 5–1 in a rematch in the group stage of the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, contributing to Spain's early exit from the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-NEDESP2014_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDESP2014-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Netherlands national football team matches have broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Nederlandse_Omroep_Stichting" title="Nederlandse Omroep Stichting">Nederlandse Omroep Stichting</a> which includes all friendlies, Nation League and <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="FIFA World Cup qualification">World Cup qualifiers</a>. The newest contract is a four-year deal until 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadiums">Stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_ArenA1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Amsterdam_ArenA1.jpg/250px-Amsterdam_ArenA1.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Amsterdam_ArenA1.jpg/375px-Amsterdam_ArenA1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Amsterdam_ArenA1.jpg/500px-Amsterdam_ArenA1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3484" data-file-height="2053" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_ArenA1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Netherlands plays most of their matches at the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Arena" title="Johan Cruyff Arena">Johan Cruyff Arena</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Dutch national team does not have a national stadium but plays mostly at the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Arena" title="Johan Cruyff Arena">Johan Cruyff Arena</a>. It played host to the first Dutch international game back in March 29, 1997, with a <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="1998 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">1998 World Cup qualification</a> match against <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino</a> which the Netherlands won 4–0.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> It was formally called the Amsterdam Arena until 2018 when it was renamed in memory of Johan Cruyff.<sup id="cite_ref-johan-cruijff-arena-1_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johan-cruijff-arena-1-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other venues that hosted Dutch international matches include the <a href="/wiki/Feijenoord_Stadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Feijenoord Stadion">Feijenoord Stadion</a>, which hosted two Dutch matches at UEFA Euro 2000 and the final, and the <a href="/wiki/Philips_Stadion" title="Philips Stadion">Philips Stadion</a> where the national team has played a range of matches.<sup id="cite_ref-stadiums_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stadiums-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managements">Managements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Managements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Netherlands_national_football_team_managers" title="List of Netherlands national football team managers">List of Netherlands national football team managers</a></div>
<p>There has been thirty-five different managers who have taken the role as manager of the Netherlands national football team with their first manager being Cees van Hasselt in the first match against Belgium back in 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Glendenning" title="Bob Glendenning">Bob Glendenning</a> holds the record for being the longest in charge with sixteen years in charge of the national team between 1925 and 1940. He has also managed the Netherlands team the most times in history with 87 matches, twenty five more than second placed manager Dick Advocaat.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_squad">Current squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Current squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<br /><i>Caps and goals updated as of 9 September 2019, after the match against <a href="/wiki/Estonia_national_football_team" title="Estonia national football team">Estonia</a>.</i>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results_and_fixtures">Results and fixtures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Results and fixtures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl><dd><i>For all past match results of the national team, see the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team_results" title="Netherlands national football team results">team's results page</a>.</i></dd></dl>
<p>The following matches were played or are scheduled to be played by the national team in the past or in the upcoming 12 months. The time in the Netherlands is shown first. If the local time is different, it will be displayed below.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018">2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team_records_and_statistics" title="Netherlands national football team records and statistics">Netherlands national football team records and statistics</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_capped_players">Most capped players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Most capped players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wesley2012.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Wesley2012.JPG/220px-Wesley2012.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Wesley2012.JPG/330px-Wesley2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/49/Wesley2012.JPG 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="435" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wesley2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wesley Sneijder is the most capped player in the history of Netherlands with 134 caps.</div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FIFA_World_Cup">FIFA World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: FIFA World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup" title="Netherlands at the FIFA World Cup">Netherlands at the FIFA World Cup</a></div>
<p>The Netherlands' first two tournament appearances at the 1934 and the 1938 editions saw them lose their first round matches to Switzerland (1934) and Czechoslovakia (1938).<sup id="cite_ref-rsssf34_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf34-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wc38_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wc38-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After not qualifying for the next six World Cups, they qualified for the 1974 FIFA World Cup in <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>. There, with the use of "Total Football" tactics, they recorded their first win in World Cup competition against Uruguay. They qualified through to the second round where a win on the final match day secured the Netherlands a spot in the final. They lost to West Germany 2–1 with Gerd Müller scoring the winning goal for the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-74WC_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74WC-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>  The Netherlands once again made the <a href="/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1978 FIFA World Cup">1978 FIFA World Cup</a> final with the team finishing second in the group behind Peru. After finishing top of the all-European group in the second round, they met Argentina in the final. Argentina protested René van de Kerkhof's forearm plaster cast. After that protest, the game went to extra time where Argentina won 3–1 after scoring two goals in extra time.<sup id="cite_ref-78WC_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78WC-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1990 edition saw the Netherlands not win a single game throughout the tournament, scoring only two goals in the group stage. After finishing with an identical record with the Republic of Ireland, they were split by drawing of lots. The Dutch took on West Germany losing 2–1 in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OddTieBreakers_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OddTieBreakers-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rsssf90_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf90-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> 1994 saw the Netherlands knocked out in the quarter-final stage as they lost to eventual champions Brazil with <a href="/wiki/Branco_(footballer)" title="Branco (footballer)">Branco</a>'s brutal free-kick sending them out.<sup id="cite_ref-1994WC_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1994WC-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> After qualifying from their group with five points, the Dutch made the semi finals of the 1998 edition where they once again lost to the Brazilians. This time it was by penalties; Phillip Cocu and Ronald de Boer's shots missed the goal to give Brazil a spot in the final. The Netherlands went on to finish in fourth place after losing to Croatia in the third-place playoff.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006, the Netherlands made it to the round of 16 where, in what was called the "Battle of Nuremberg" they lost by a single goal to Portugal. The Dutch were given seven yellow cards.<sup id="cite_ref-Nuremberg_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nuremberg-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The following edition, in 2010, saw the team qualify to the knockout stage by finishing atop Group E. After defeating Slovakia 2–1 in the round of 16, they came back from an early goal by <a href="/wiki/Robinho" title="Robinho">Robinho</a> to defeat Brazil 2–1 in the quarter-finals as Wesley Sneijder scored a double.<sup id="cite_ref-NEDVSSVK_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDVSSVK-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NEDVSBRA_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDVSBRA-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In the semi-final, they defeated Uruguay in a tough game for the Dutch, making their first World Cup final since 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In the final, they took on Spain. During normal time, the Dutch had plenty of chances to win the game, the closest being in the 62nd minute when Sneijder shot wide. Spain's winning goal came off a play in the 116th minute after the Netherlands went down to ten men.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2010WCF_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010WCF-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, the Netherlands finish atop Group B with wins over Spain, Australia and Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-WC2014_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WC2014-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In the round of 16 match against Mexico, the Netherlands came back from a goal down to manage a 2–1 win in stoppage time with Klaas-Jan Huntelaar scoring a controversial penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-NEDvMEX_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDvMEX-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In the quarter-finals, they defeated Costa Rica on penalties however they lost to Argentina on penalties in the semi-final.<sup id="cite_ref-CRCvNED_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRCvNED-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%; text-align:center;">

<p><i>Football at the Summer Olympics has been an under-23 tournament since 1992 (with three players of over 23 years of age allowed in the squad).</i>

<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that this match is not considered to be a full international by the English <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">Football Association</a>, and does not appear in the records of the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England team</a>, because professional football had already been introduced in England at that time. In the Netherlands, however, professional football was not introduced until 1954. Before then, players who left the Netherlands to turn pro in another country were banned from the national team.</span>
